<span id="freeTextContainer2969226149428978879"><p> <em>“Remember, what’s down inside you, all covered up—the things of your soul. The important, secret things . . . The story of you, all buried, let the music caress it out into the open.”</em> </p><p>When Allegra was a little girl, she thought she would pick up her violin and it would sing for her—that the music was hidden inside her instrument.<br /> Now that Allegra is twelve, she believes t</p></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2969226149428978879"><p>
  <em>“Remember, what’s down inside you, all covered up—the things of your soul. The important, secret things . . . The story of you, all buried, let the music caress it out into the open.”</em>
</p><p>When Allegra was a little girl, she thought she would pick up her violin and it would sing for her—that the music was hidden inside her instrument.<br />     Now that Allegra is twelve, she believes the music is in her fingers, and the summer after seventh grade she has to teach them well. She’s the youngest contestant in the Ernest Bloch Young Musicians’ Competition.<br />     She knows she will learn the notes to the concerto, but what she doesn’t realize is she’ll also learn—how to close the gap between herself and Mozart to find the real music inside her heart.</p></span>

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/965766-tracy?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer287520431">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11536769047037870732">This story is slow and contemplative. The beginning was a bit odd and almost too slow, but by the end I was completely absorbed and utterly satisfied. <br /><br />The book caught my attention because it is about a 12 year old girl who plays both softball and the violin. I have an almost-12 year old daughter who does both of those things, too, so I picked it up to see if it would interest her. The book was published in 1991, so the voice may not be modern or exciting enough to engage today's youth. I will re</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11536769047037870732">This story is slow and contemplative. The beginning was a bit odd and almost too slow, but by the end I was completely absorbed and utterly satisfied. <br /><br />The book caught my attention because it is about a 12 year old girl who plays both softball and the violin. I have an almost-12 year old daughter who does both of those things, too, so I picked it up to see if it would interest her. The book was published in 1991, so the voice may not be modern or exciting enough to engage today's youth. I will recommend it to my daughter, and I'll probably even buy a copy to have on our shelves, but she will probably not stick with it. <br /><br />One thing I deeply appreciated in this story was the fact that even though this 12 year old girl is an immensely talented violinist, possibly even a prodigy, her parents and her violin teacher are completely relaxed about the whole thing. There is no carrying on about her gift, or her obligations; they encourage her to play because she loves it, they encourage her to enjoy it. They let her make her own decisions about where this gift is going to take her. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11536769047037870732">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer253648171">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13667445976481956040">This book dances and sings, even as the characters mourn for lost music, and lost lives. 12-year-old Leah is a prodigy, the youngest finalist in a prestigious violin competition. She’s very mature – at times she seems a better fit for graduate school than middle school – but she still has a young girl’s dreams and inspirations, along with an eye and ear for all the distracting details that wedge themselves into her day. <br /><br />I like the asides of music history: André Previn writing for Itzhak Perlman’</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13667445976481956040">This book dances and sings, even as the characters mourn for lost music, and lost lives. 12-year-old Leah is a prodigy, the youngest finalist in a prestigious violin competition. She’s very mature – at times she seems a better fit for graduate school than middle school – but she still has a young girl’s dreams and inspirations, along with an eye and ear for all the distracting details that wedge themselves into her day. <br /><br />I like the asides of music history: André Previn writing for Itzhak Perlman’s baby, Ernest Chausson biking into a stone wall. And the letter from Bubbe Raisa is a lyric tragedy. <br /><br />Thankfully, Wolff’s dominant tones are joyous and beautiful. This book makes me happy to feel whatever there is to feel, happy to be alive. </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer484526208">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16597541099918154437">Allegra is a talented musician. She’s played the violin for several years and plays very well. She is selected to be a finalist in the Bloch Competition, but just playing notes won’t get her first prize. Allegra has to realize that the music is not in her fingers, but inside her heart.<br /><br />I was able to relate to Allegra. I understood her struggles because I had the same problem a few years ago. I believed the music was in my fingers and that’s how I played. Eventually, I realized that I had to reach</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16597541099918154437">Allegra is a talented musician. She’s played the violin for several years and plays very well. She is selected to be a finalist in the Bloch Competition, but just playing notes won’t get her first prize. Allegra has to realize that the music is not in her fingers, but inside her heart.<br /><br />I was able to relate to Allegra. I understood her struggles because I had the same problem a few years ago. I believed the music was in my fingers and that’s how I played. Eventually, I realized that I had to reach into my own heart, find the music, and allow to flow out. <br /><br />I would recommend this book to young musicians. They would certianly appreciate it more and be able to relate to Allegra's struggles. I truly enjoyed this book!<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11073432719388583586">Again, a book I chose to read for my Humanities class.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText11073432719388583586">Again, a book I chose to read for my Humanities class. They all seem to be the same: the beginning irritates me, and barely manages to hold my attention, but by the end I'm crying and smiling about the way it has progressed. This story is about a girl Allegra Shapiro and her summer journey through training for a violin competition. It definitely made me want to pick up my flute, or sax, or guitar, or even plunk away at the piano. I found I could relate by the end when she finally decides to play the competition "for her grandmother". I can't think of a time I step on stage, or play any form of music that I don't think of my Grandparents. Both my great-grandmother, and my grandma. It's a very sweet book, and I quite liked it. =]</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1036595666">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1036595666" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/34247539-magdiel-a" class="left imgcol" title="Magdiel A."><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1428638014p2/34247539.jpg" alt="Magdiel A." /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1036595666?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 26, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/34247539-magdiel-a" class="user" title="Magdiel A.">Magdiel A.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/827988.The_Mozart_Season" title="Paperback 9780312367459" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/34247539-magdiel-a?shelf=badreads" class="actionLinkLite">badreads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1036595666">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5252107852593615080">The Mozart Season is a surprisingly brief book concerning a young and marvelous violinist, Allegra Leah Shapiro, who is quite outstanding and skillful at music. By virtue of possessing these impressive skills, she was selected from a field of eighty-five to engage in the Ernest Bloch Competition for Young Musicians of Oregon and play a Mozart concerto. But great honor comes with great sacrifice. Allegra must spend the rest of her summer in the company of this concerto, attempting to play its mos</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5252107852593615080">The Mozart Season is a surprisingly brief book concerning a young and marvelous violinist, Allegra Leah Shapiro, who is quite outstanding and skillful at music. By virtue of possessing these impressive skills, she was selected from a field of eighty-five to engage in the Ernest Bloch Competition for Young Musicians of Oregon and play a Mozart concerto. But great honor comes with great sacrifice. Allegra must spend the rest of her summer in the company of this concerto, attempting to play its most accurate version, as to honor the former writer of this composition; the eccentric, troubled, and young Mozart. Throughout this peculiar summer, young Allegra will evolve not only into a more respected musician, but also into a more sophisticated, mature, and confident individual. Far and wide this novel Shapiro will experience the repercussions of her ancestry and its legacy to her, the struggle of commemorating a piece and its compositor instead of overpowering him, the encounter of an odd woman who’ll help her initiate in her endless journey of finding herself, a lost man restlessly seeking his lost song, among other miscellaneous yet innovating undertakings. <br /><br />I’m going to say right off the bat that I found this book thought-provoking yet tedious, dull, and monotonous. I couldn't stand Allegra and the slow progress made in both her music and the development of her reflections or thoughts. This book was hard to grasp without being easily distracted or falling asleep, in behalf of how the author lacks the strength and will to hook or engage the reader into the story or the evolution of its plot and characters. I take my hat off for the clever way in which she plays with words, and the way she Capitalizes Some Words is rather amusing. And also the proper use of italic is absolutely relishing. Despite the fact of having a witty word choice, and a great message to the reader in the surface, the author didn't manage to thread these fine ideas into neither captivating words or plot. Although of the things afore mentioned, I must give credit to the author for taking her time in describing and defining musical terms to help the reader understand and keep up with Allegra’s advanced music knowledge. This gave the story a polished impression. My verdict? A fine, thought-provoking book, but undeniably not one of my favorites.<br /><br /><strong>[<u>This review was published</u> on my <em>Teen Ink</em> account. To visit this page, and check my review on this Teen magazine with Editor's Choice award, please click <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.teenink.com/reviews/book_reviews/article/705663/The-Mozart-Season-by-Virginia-Euwer-Wolff/">here</a>.]</strong><br /><br />As to <em>avoid comments claiming I didn't write this!</em> Thanks. :) </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5252107852593615080">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText362952905786707947">Ignorant me believed this was classic novelist Virginia Woolf when coming across it in the "give a book/take a book" box. Not too belatedly realized it was a young adult novel written and set in the early 90's. <br /><br />It is, however, a thoughtful story of a teenage girl in love with music and her violin that would appeal to anyone of any age. I do wish the book had been around when I was a teenager.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText17172267771610107854">This would most likely appeal to those who study the violin - so a small subset of readers. I've studied music a long time, so it was somewhat interesting to me - but not sure how much it would appeal to most middle school girls. Not for ELL students - vocabulary too specialized- not high enough interest. <br /><br />However there were some great lines - more to do with the mindset of how one recreates a piece of music to make it individualized to the player while acknowledging the writer/creator of the piece. That was completely fascinating to me.<br /><br />"How to move so close to it that there would be just that edge Mr. Kaplan talked about - How to get something strung just right in me so I'd be balancing right exactly on that edge - How to remember everything I know and forget it at the same time and invent a new thing. And that would be the way to let music out of me." (92)<br /><br />"Daddy, is everything a matter of life or death?"..."The evidence is right here, right now. Suffering and joy. That's all there is. There isn't anything else. And they're so close together...it strikes terror in the human soul." (p. 152). Actually - I disagree - for many people life is more like T.S. Eliot's "The Hollow Men". Still it made me think.<br /><br />"This piece (by Sibelius- which one?)...has a profound yearning and a profound lament - at the same time. Like life. Let's play." (156)<br /><br />"Well, what do you think pain's supposed to mean?"..."Oh, I don't know...I do know it connects the whole human species...I just don't know why." (It also is a part of animals' lives...obviously- but I don't think it connects them - Don't mind me, I'm just arguing with the text).</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText305449658482368132">If you're the type of teacher who tells students to give it 110%, Virginia Euwer Wolff would like to have a word with you.<br /><br />A few "notes" (pun intended):<br />- This book came out before Allegra the allergy medication did. So when I saw the commercial for Allegra, The Mozart Season came to mind, haha<br />- For those of you who are familiar with neither Italian nor musical markings, "Allegro" doesn't mean "fast" in Italian but is the marking used for a piece that is played fast. Clearly Ms. Wolff was thinking of this when she decided on Allegra as the name of her protagonist. At least that's what it looks like...<br />- When she's not practicing her violin, Allegra is out and about riding her bike, catching an outdoor concert on a warm summer day, and listening to jazz. There's even a recipe in the book. There are of course other features, but these are my recollections after not having read the book for 15+ years. That's a long time dude...<br />- This is a young adult book intended for a sixth-grade audience, according to the book itself. I would take this with a grain of salt however, being that even as an eighth grader, I couldn't fully comprehend the book. What can I say, reading comprehension isn't exactly my... FORTE. *snort* I know, I know...</span>

          <a href="/book/show/827988.The_Mozart_Season" title="Paperback 9780312367459" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Lisa, Toby, Kezia, Deborah</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2807810-phoebe?shelf=ya" class="actionLinkLite">ya</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2807810-phoebe?shelf=realistic-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2807810-phoebe?shelf=contemporary" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer503179136">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4079498046739573671">Though this novel begins slowly, it is a beautifully written effort that really wows. Allegra Shapiro looks forward to the summer after 7th grade, since softball is over and she can get back to concentrating on violin. Then her music teacher tells her that she is a finalist (and the youngest one) in the Bloch competition for young musicians, which will be held in September. This staggering news colors Allegra's life from then on, and the transformations she goes through during the summer, in res</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4079498046739573671">Though this novel begins slowly, it is a beautifully written effort that really wows. Allegra Shapiro looks forward to the summer after 7th grade, since softball is over and she can get back to concentrating on violin. Then her music teacher tells her that she is a finalist (and the youngest one) in the Bloch competition for young musicians, which will be held in September. This staggering news colors Allegra's life from then on, and the transformations she goes through during the summer, in response to a variety of events, are marvelously voiced in her clear, intelligent way. Everything she experiences that summer feeds into her final interpretation of the piece she must play for the competition (Mozart's Fourth Concerto in D). She is only 12, and brilliant, but also very normal, and kids should warm to her. I loved the way Wolff writes about music, despite some technicality, and about life, and family, and the people who have gone before. This is an extraordinary, masterful novel and I don't know why it was skipped for any Newbery mention back in 1992. Junior high, up.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4079498046739573671">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17895397233385300430">The story is based on Allegra Shapiro, a twelve year old violinist. One day, she gets into a competition, but she loses. Her friend, Mr. Trouble is trying to identify a song he has in his head. At the end of the story, he identifies the song with Allegra's help. Allegra is happy for Mr.Trouble and forgets her disappointment with the competition. <br />I especially liked the book because it was written in first person. I was able to understand the feelings of a good violinist. For example, when the orc</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17895397233385300430">The story is based on Allegra Shapiro, a twelve year old violinist. One day, she gets into a competition, but she loses. Her friend, Mr. Trouble is trying to identify a song he has in his head. At the end of the story, he identifies the song with Allegra's help. Allegra is happy for Mr.Trouble and forgets her disappointment with the competition. <br />I especially liked the book because it was written in first person. I was able to understand the feelings of a good violinist. For example, when the orchestra was tuning, Allegra realized that some players had tuned incorrectly. Almost everyone in Allegra's family could play an instrument. When they have family conversation, it always relates to music. This is completely different from my family's conversations. I also learned more about reading music scores. When Allegra thought about the Mozart violin concertos, I learned new facts about the composer and about the music. I would recommend this book to people who like classical music.</span>

First, the author wrote characters that I could relate with like the main character. We both are musicians and we both know a lot about music. Second, I really liked the plot of the story.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText9342217898484321220">The Mozart Season was a fantastic book for me and I absolutely loved it!!!! First, the author wrote characters that I could relate with like the main character. We both are musicians and we both know a lot about music. Second, I really liked the plot of the story. The main character had to practice to get a spot for her spotlight symphony solo. Thirdly, the supporting characters was a great part to the story. The parents and the private lesson teacher gave interesting points about music and interesting points that affected the main character. Finally, I loved the resolution of the story.   <div class="xhr_comment_photo">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1287594245">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14182358304429997037">This book seemed to be written for a young adult audience. A little simple, but a fairly good story. I read this book afyer lending it to my mother to read. It was the last book she read before she passed away. She didn't want to read any books with murder (cozy mystery or not) so I found this one on my shelf and shared it with her. She enjoyed it.</span>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5488687-ameliedanjou?shelf=music-poetry" class="actionLinkLite">music-poetry</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5488687-ameliedanjou?shelf=ya-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">ya-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer862464227">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2646271453831276781">If you were a practicing musician in your youth, then this book is for you, especially if you are/were a violinist. I really felt that I knew the main character -- she wasn't me (I never practiced that much, but had friends who did), but might have been my stand partner. (No, honestly, she was sitting a couple stands up.) Not for everyone, but some of us will truly enjoy it.<br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_454825927">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/454825927" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/13160149-jillian" class="left imgcol" title="Jillian"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1350796855p2/13160149.jpg" alt="Jillian" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/454825927?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 20, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/13160149-jillian" class="user" title="Jillian">Jillian</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/827988.The_Mozart_Season" title="Paperback 9780312367459" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer454825927">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5772988054906545381">Anyone who wants a glimpse inside the agony and joy of a musician as she practices and performs should read this book.<br /><br />This is an extremely unusual young adult novel. The plot is based in routine rather than action, and the protagonist is unabashedly contemplative and intelligent. She is also refreshingly open to people who are different (perhaps because she can relate) and seldom has anything negative to say about the other characters. Although the book was not "perfect," I loved the way the cha</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5772988054906545381">Anyone who wants a glimpse inside the agony and joy of a musician as she practices and performs should read this book.<br /><br />This is an extremely unusual young adult novel. The plot is based in routine rather than action, and the protagonist is unabashedly contemplative and intelligent. She is also refreshingly open to people who are different (perhaps because she can relate) and seldom has anything negative to say about the other characters. Although the book was not "perfect," I loved the way the characters thought about, practiced, and performed music. Throughout the book, Allegra demonstrates how a piece of music can change a musician's understanding of life, and how a musician's life affects her relationship with the music.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5772988054906545381">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_49103441">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49103441" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/689186-todd" class="left imgcol" title="Todd"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1231557036p2/689186.jpg" alt="Todd" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/49103441?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 21, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/689186-todd" class="user" title="Todd">Todd</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">classical music enthusiasts</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/689186-todd?shelf=10s-11s" class="actionLinkLite">10s-11s</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/689186-todd?shelf=12s-13s" class="actionLinkLite">12s-13s</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/689186-todd?shelf=extra-shelf" class="actionLinkLite">extra-shelf</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/689186-todd?shelf=10s-11s-contemporary-realistic" class="actionLinkLite">10s-11s-contemporary-realistic</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/689186-todd?shelf=12s-13s-contemporary-realistic" class="actionLinkLite">12s-13s-contemporary-realistic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer49103441">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8567774706153225426">I was pretty lukewarm about this book for the first third but then it turned a quiet corner. Protagonist isn't an orphan or a victim or poor or even losing a friend. She's 12 and has parents who love her dearly and she lives in a world of classical music—not because she's some kind of prodigy but because it runs in the family. All of which is a kind of normalcy I find refreshing. I'm a sucker for books that explore the creative process and this one nicely gives you a peek inside the head of a yo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8567774706153225426">I was pretty lukewarm about this book for the first third but then it turned a quiet corner. Protagonist isn't an orphan or a victim or poor or even losing a friend. She's 12 and has parents who love her dearly and she lives in a world of classical music—not because she's some kind of prodigy but because it runs in the family. All of which is a kind of normalcy I find refreshing. I'm a sucker for books that explore the creative process and this one nicely gives you a peek inside the head of a young violinist preparing for her first big contest but also trying to understand her heritage as she grows up. Some flashback repetition gets a little tedious but something stayed honest throughout.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8567774706153225426">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/1977375-leeann" class="left imgcol" title="Leeann"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Leeann" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1233611331?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 15, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1977375-leeann" class="user" title="Leeann">Leeann</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/827988.The_Mozart_Season" title="Paperback 9780312367459" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1233611331">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15185710265969937943">I have such mixed emotions about this book. I struggled to be enthralled for the first half. I questioned the unique relationships in the story. I wondered how a twelve-year-old could be expected to handle such mature emotions as well as being asked to dig deep within her own young soul to give meaning to a Mozart concerto. I also thought it was curious how Allegra gave the term "genius" to the other competitors but failed to see her own genius. However, in spite of all of these feelings and que</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15185710265969937943">I have such mixed emotions about this book. I struggled to be enthralled for the first half. I questioned the unique relationships in the story. I wondered how a twelve-year-old could be expected to handle such mature emotions as well as being asked to dig deep within her own young soul to give meaning to a Mozart concerto. I also thought it was curious how Allegra gave the term "genius" to the other competitors but failed to see her own genius. However, in spite of all of these feelings and questions on my part as a reader, I thought this was a beautiful, thoughtful story and found it to be well worth the effort of sticking with it to the end.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15185710265969937943">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer17745992">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4444888491985572788">I play the violin, but as violin players go, I'm totally a hack (I'm one of those adult amateurs that Allegra's teacher warns her about because they always play the sixteenth notes too fast). I read this book a few years ago, and the idea of great music being a lessening of the distance between the composer and musician resonated with me a lot. After this reading, I think what will stick in my head is what Deidre said, about how in music you have to simultaneously remember everything, and forget</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4444888491985572788">I play the violin, but as violin players go, I'm totally a hack (I'm one of those adult amateurs that Allegra's teacher warns her about because they always play the sixteenth notes too fast). I read this book a few years ago, and the idea of great music being a lessening of the distance between the composer and musician resonated with me a lot. After this reading, I think what will stick in my head is what Deidre said, about how in music you have to simultaneously remember everything, and forget, the divine power of the NBA. Great book for musicians, and I wrote down Allegra's oatmeal recipe.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_9413110">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9413110" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/75209-megan" class="left imgcol" title="Megan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1437244843p2/75209.jpg" alt="Megan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/9413110?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 21, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/75209-megan" class="user" title="Megan">Megan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those who like good stories</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/75209-megan?shelf=kidbooks" class="actionLinkLite">kidbooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer9413110">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer523884032963982605">This story takes place in Portland over the course of a summer. The very simple premise is that life takes on seasons, and for Allegra this summer will be a Mozart season as she prepares for a competition. We watch Mozart and Allegra affect each other and meet wonderful characters who have also been deeply changed by the role of music in their lives. My favorite is the homeless man who lost his "Waltz Tree" many years ago and travels from one free city concert to the next looking for it. The sto</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText523884032963982605">This story takes place in Portland over the course of a summer. The very simple premise is that life takes on seasons, and for Allegra this summer will be a Mozart season as she prepares for a competition. We watch Mozart and Allegra affect each other and meet wonderful characters who have also been deeply changed by the role of music in their lives. My favorite is the homeless man who lost his "Waltz Tree" many years ago and travels from one free city concert to the next looking for it. The story is so well written I was extremely sad (yet satisfied)when it was finished. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="523884032963982605">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kk86cKbyNZwIJe6Bt67/tg7RvpJ3Fdx9OhQKuVRg2533mwWjVCAhZoT9mjrJzxkERyZ9iz7Im9dQHQ8rmPUt2A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

In the course of his long career in the northern Italian city of Cremona, he created more than a thousand stringed instruments; approximately six hundred survive, their quality unequalled by any subsequent violin-maker. In this fascinating book, Toby Faber traces the rich, multilayered stories of six of these peerless creations–five violins and a cello–and the one towering artist who brought them into being. Blending history, biography, meticulous detective work, and an abiding passion for music, Faber takes us from the salons of Vienna to the concert halls of New York, and from the breakthroughs of Beethoven’s last quartets to the first phonographic recordings. At sixteen, when she made her professional debut, she was hailed as one of the world\'s most talented and exciting musicians. But ten years later, she stopped playing virtually overnight, when multiple sclerosis removed the feeling in her hands just before a concert. It took fourteen more years for the crippling disease to take its final toll.In this uniquely revealing biography, Hilary and Piers du Pré have re-created the life they shared with their sister in astonishing personal detail, unveiling the private world behind the public face. With warmth and candor they recount Jackie\'s blissful love of the cello, her marriage to the conductor Daniel Barenboim, her compulsions, her suffering, and, above all, the price exacted by her talent on the whole family.
